A) Because insanity is a legal restriction (hajr) on statements.
B) Because the pillar of contract (aqd) and performance (ada') are missing.
C) Because the insane cannot intend faith.
D) Because faith is not legislated for the insane.

Key Takeaway
Insanity does not negate capacity for obligation (ahliyyat al-wujub) because the dhimma remains, but it restricts performance capacity except in rights of people.

Effects of Legal Incapacity on Obligations
Explains how incapacity affects liability and obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi usul rule that childhood (siba) removes liability (uhdah) for acts of worship and distinguish between pure and mixed liability.

Core Idea
Legal incapacity removes liability (uhdah) but does not invalidate the act; rights of Allah can excuse forgetfulness, but human rights cannot.

This passage from al-Pazdawi's Usul explains how various states of legal incapacity—childhood, mental deficiency, forgetfulness, and sleep—affect religious obligations. We'll unpack the key concept of uhdah (liability) and see how the Hanafi school distinguishes between rights of Allah and rights of people in forgiving forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the example of a child's faith
Read the opening: why is a child's faith considered fard, not nafl? Note the reasoning that if it were nafl, it would not suffice for the obligatory upon puberty.
This is a key illustration of how the Hanafis derive rules from practical consequences.
2
Define uhdah and its two types
Identify the Arabic term 'al-uhdah' and note the two categories: pure (khalisah) and mixed (mashubah). Understand that childhood removes pure liability but only suspends mixed liability pending guardian consent.
Mixed liability includes financial transactions and marriage contracts.
3
Compare childhood with insanity and mental deficiency
Childhood (siba) and insanity after puberty ('utah) both prevent liability but do not invalidate speech/action. However, insanity is not time-limited, so some rulings (e.g., response to wife's conversion) are not delayed.
Sane child and sane mentally deficient person are treated alike.
4
Analyze forgetfulness
Forgetfulness does not negate wujub in rights of Allah but can be an excuse if predominant (e.g., fasting, tasmiya). In rights of people, forgetfulness is never an excuse.
The distinction is based on rights of Allah being a trial (ibtila') and human rights being based on need (hajah).
5
Examine sleep as a temporary incapacity
Sleep is an inability to use one's capacity, delaying performance but not removing obligation because it is temporary.
Contrast with childhood and insanity which are prolonged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان، حتى إذا أداه : كان فرضاً، لا نفلاً.
ألا يُرى أنه إذا آمن في صغره لزمه أحكام تثبت بناءً على صحة الإيمان، وهي جعلت تبعاً للإيمان الفرض.
ولذلك إذا بلغ ولم يُعد كلمة الشهادة: لم يُجعل مرتداً، ولو كان الأول نفلاً لما أجزأ عن الفرض، ووضع عنه التكليف، وإلزام الأداء. : وجملة الأمر ما قلنا أن توضع عنه العهدة، وتصح منه، وله ما لا عهدة فيه؛ لأن الصبا من أسباب المرحمة، فجعل سبباً للعفو عن كل عهدة تحتمل العفو
ولذلك لا يُحرَمُ الميراث بالقتل، ولا يلزم عليه حرمانه عنه بالكفر، والرق؛ لأن الرق ينافي أهلية الإرث وكذلك الكفر؛ لأنه ينافي أهلية الولاية، وانعدام الحق لعدم سببه ، أو عدم أهليته : لا يُعدُّ جزاء.
والعهدة نوعان:
خالصة لا تلزم الصبي بحال.
ومَشُوبةٌ يتوقف لزومها على رأي الولي، ولما كان الصبا عجزاً: صار من أسباب ولاية النظر، وقطع ولايته عن الأغيار.
وأما العته بعد البلوغ : فمثل الصبا مع العقل في كل الأحكام، حتى إنه لا يمنع صحة القول والفعل، لكنه يمنع العهدة.
وأما ضمان ما يستهلك من الأموال فليس بعهدة، لكنه شرع جبراً، وكونه صبياً معذوراً ، أو معتوهاً : لا ينافي عصمة المحل، ويوضع الخطاب عنه كما وُضع عن الصبي، ويولَّى عليه، ولا يلي على غيره.
وإنما يفترق الجنون والصغر : في أن هذا العارض غير محدود، فقيل: إذا أسلمت امرأته عُرض على أبيه الإسلام، أو على أمه، ولا يؤخَّر، والصبا محدود، فوجب تأخيره.
وأما الصبي العاقل، والمعتوه العاقل : فلا يفترقان
وأما النسيان : فلا ينافي الوجوب في حق الله تعالى، ولكنه يحتمل أن يُجعل عذراً، وفي حقوق العباد لا يُجعل عذراً؛ لأن حقوق العباد محترمة؛ لحقهم وحاجتهم لا ابتلاء، وحقوق الله تعالى ابتلاء، لكن النسيان إذا كان غالباً : يلازم الطاعة إما بطريق الدعوة، مثل النسيان في الصوم، وإما باعتبار حال البشر، مثل التسمية في الذبيحة، جعل من أسباب العفو في حق الله تعالى؛ لأنه من جهة صاحب الحق اعترض، فجعل سبباً للعفو في حقه.
بخلاف حقوق العباد ؛ لأن النسيان ليس بعذر من جهتهم.
والنسيان ضربان ضرب أصلي، وضرب يقع فيه المرء بالتقصير، وهذا يصلح للعتاب.
والنسيان في غير الصوم: لم يُجعل عذراً.
وكذلك في غير الذبيحة ؛ لأنه ليس مثل المنصوص عليه في غلبة الوجود، فبطلت التعدية، حتى إن سلام الناسي لما كان غالباً: عُدَّ عذراً.
وأما النوم : فعَجز عن استعمال قدرة الأحوال، فأوجب تأخير الخطاب للأداء، ولم يمنع الوجوب لاحتمال الأداء؛ لأن النوم لا يمتد،
Faith, even if he performs it: it was an obligation, not a supererogatory act. Do you not see that if he believes in his childhood, rulings are established based on the validity of faith, and these rulings are made dependent on the obligatory faith. Therefore, if he reaches puberty and does not repeat the declaration of faith, he is not considered an apostate. And if the first [faith] were supererogatory, it would not suffice for the obligatory, and responsibility would be removed from him and the obligation of performance removed. The summary is what we said: that liability is removed from him, and it is valid from him, and he has that which has no liability; because childhood is among the causes of mercy, so it is made a cause for pardon from every liability that can bear pardon. Therefore, he is not deprived of inheritance by killing, nor is deprivation from him required due to disbelief or slavery; because slavery is incompatible with the capacity for inheritance, and likewise disbelief because it is incompatible with the capacity for guardianship. And the absence of a right due to the absence of its cause or its capacity: is not considered a punishment. Liability is of two types: pure liability that does not bind the child at all; and mixed liability whose binding depends on the guardian's opinion. Since childhood is an incapacity, it became a cause for the guardianship of oversight, and it cuts off his authority over others. As for insanity after puberty: it is like childhood along with reason in all rulings, such that it does not prevent the validity of speech and action, but it prevents liability. As for the guarantee of wealth that is consumed, it is not liability, but it is legislated as a compensatory measure. And his being a child excused or insane does not contradict the sanctity of the subject of liability, and address is removed from him as it is removed from a child, and he is placed under guardianship and does not have guardianship over others. The difference between insanity and childhood is that this hindrance is not limited. So it is said: If his wife becomes Muslim, Islam is presented to his father or to his mother, and it is not delayed. But childhood is limited, so it must be delayed. As for the sane child and the sane mentally deficient person, they do not differ. As for forgetfulness: it does not negate obligation with respect to the rights of Allah, but it can be considered an excuse. In the rights of people, it is not considered an excuse because the rights of people are respected due to their right and need, not as a trial. And the rights of Allah are a trial. However, if forgetfulness is predominant, it is associated with obedience either by way of calling, like forgetfulness in fasting, or by considering the human condition, like the mention of Allah's name at slaughter, it is made a cause of pardon with respect to the rights of Allah because it arises from the side of the right-holder, so it is made a cause for pardon in His right. Unlike the rights of people, because forgetfulness is not an excuse from their side. And forgetfulness is of two types: original forgetfulness and forgetfulness that occurs due to negligence; this last is subject to reprimand. Forgetfulness in other than fasting is not made an excuse. Likewise in other than slaughter; because it is not like the textually specified case in terms of predominant occurrence, so analogy is invalidated. Thus, since forgetting the greeting of salam is predominant, it is counted as an excuse. As for sleep: it is an inability to use one's capacity over conditions, so it necessitates deferring the address for performance, but it does not negate obligation due to the possibility of performance, because sleep does not last long.
Source pages p. 726

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of legal incapacity (siba, junun, 'utah, nisyan, nawm) on taklif (obligation) and uhdah (liability). It begins with the example of a child's faith (iman): if a child believes, it is considered valid and obligatory (fard) upon him, not supererogatory (nafl). This is proven by the fact that after puberty he is not asked to repeat the shahada; if his childhood faith were merely supererogatory, it would not suffice for the obligatory duty upon maturity. Therefore, the ruling is that childhood (siba) removes liability (uhdah) for acts of worship because it is a cause of mercy (rahma). The author defines two types of uhdah: pure liability (which does not bind the child at all) and mixed liability (which depends on the guardian's consent, e.g., financial transactions). Childhood is considered an incapacity that gives guardianship (wilaya) to the guardian over the child. Insanity after puberty ('utah) is similar to childhood with reason: it does not prevent valid speech/action but prevents liability. However, compensation for consumption of wealth (daman) is not liability but a compensatory obligation that remains even for the insane/child because the subject is protected. The difference between insanity and childhood is that insanity is not limited in time, so if an insane man's wife converts to Islam, Islam is presented to his father/mother without delay; but childhood is limited, so it is delayed until puberty. The discussion then turns to forgetfulness (nisyan): it does not remove the obligation of rights of Allah (huquq Allah) but can be an excuse in some cases like forgetfulness in fasting or forgetting the basmala in slaughter, because these are predominant forgetfulness. For human rights, forgetfulness is generally not an excuse because human rights are based on need, not trial. Forgetfulness due to negligence is blameworthy. Sleep (nawm) is a temporary incapacity that delays performance but does not negate obligation, as sleep is not prolonged.

Key Terms
العهدة (al-uhdah): Liability or responsibility for fulfilling an obligation, which can be pure (binding) or mixed (dependent on guardian).
الصبا (al-siba): Childhood, a period of legal incapacity considered a cause of mercy that removes liability except for basic acts.
العته (al-utah): Mental deficiency short of insanity that occurs after puberty, similar to childhood but with reason; it prevents liability but not validity of speech/action.
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness that does not negate obligation but can be an excuse in certain matters of Allah's rights due to predominant occurrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of forgetfulness is not excused?
A) Forgetfulness in fasting
B) Forgetfulness in greeting with salam
C) Forgetfulness in rights of people
D) Forgetfulness in tasmiya

Key Takeaway
Legal incapacity (siba, 'utah, nisyan, nawm) affects liability (uhdah) differently: some remove uhdah entirely, some only delay, and some do not affect wujub but may excuse performance in rights of Allah.

The Legal Effect of Forgetfulness
Definition and classification of nisyan in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal effect of forgetfulness (nisyan) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and distinguish the two types of forgetfulness based on prevalence and negligence.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness does not lift obligation but may excuse in Allah's rights if prevalent.

In this passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul, we examine forgetfulness (nisyan) as an impediment (mani') that does not negate the obligation itself but may serve as an excuse under certain conditions. The Hanafi school distinguishes between rights of Allah and rights of people, and further classifies forgetfulness into original and negligence-based types. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying rulings correctly in ibadat and muamalat.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify that nisyan does not negate obligation in Allah's rights but may be an excuse; in people's rights it is not an excuse.
The text begins with 'wa amma al-nisyan: fala yunafi al-wujub...'
2
Identify the rationale for the distinction
Rights of Allah are a trial (ibtilā'), while people's rights are for their benefit and are respected.
Rights of Allah are abrogated by forgetfulness; people's rights are not.
3
Note the condition of prevalence (ghalaba)
Forgetfulness is excused in Allah's rights only when it is prevalent (ghalib), as in fasting and slaughter.
If forgetfulness is rare, it is not an excuse.
4
Distinguish the two types of forgetfulness
Original (asli) forgetfulness is involuntary and excusable; negligence-based (taqsir) forgetfulness is blameworthy and not excusable.
The text says 'al-nisyan darban darb asli wa darb yuqa' fihi al-mar' bi al-taqsir'
5
Understand the examples and limitation of analogical extension
Examples: forgetfulness in fasting and saying Bismillah in slaughter are excused due to prevalence. Analogical extension to other cases is invalid because prevalence is not the same.
The text explicitly rejects qiyas for other cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النسيان : فلا ينافي الوجوب في حق الله تعالى، ولكنه يحتمل أن يُجعل عذراً، وفي حقوق العباد لا يُجعل عذراً؛ لأن حقوق العباد محترمة؛ لحقهم وحاجتهم لا ابتلاء، وحقوق الله تعالى ابتلاء، لكن النسيان إذا كان غالباً : يلازم الطاعة إما بطريق الدعوة، مثل النسيان في الصوم، وإما باعتبار حال البشر، مثل التسمية في الذبيحة، جعل من أسباب العفو في حق الله تعالى؛ لأنه من جهة صاحب الحق اعترض، فجعل سبباً للعفو في حقه. بخلاف حقوق العباد ؛ لأن النسيان ليس بعذر من جهتهم. والنسيان ضربان ضرب أصلي، وضرب يقع فيه المرء بالتقصير، وهذا يصلح للعتاب. والنسيان في غير الصوم: لم يُجعل عذراً. وكذلك في غير الذبيحة ؛ لأنه ليس مثل المنصوص عليه في غلبة الوجود، فبطلت التعدية، حتى إن سلام الناسي لما كان غالباً: عُدَّ عذراً.
As for forgetfulness: it does not negate obligation in the rights of Allah the Most High, but it is possible to be made an excuse. In the rights of people, it is not made an excuse, because the rights of people are respected due to their right and need, not as a trial, while the rights of Allah are a trial. However, if forgetfulness is prevalent, it accompanies obedience either by way of calling [to worship], like forgetfulness in fasting, or by considering human condition, like the Basmalah in slaughter, it is made a cause of pardon in the rights of Allah, because from the perspective of the owner of the right it occurs, so it is made a cause of pardon regarding His right. Contrary to the rights of people, because forgetfulness is not an excuse from their side. Forgetfulness is of two types: an original type, and a type that occurs due to negligence, and this is suitable for reproach. Forgetfulness in other than fasting was not made an excuse. Likewise in other than slaughter, because it is not like the text regarding prevalence, so analogical extension is invalid. Even the greeting of the forgetful person, because it is prevalent, was considered an excuse.
Source pages p. 727

Commentary
This passage discusses the impediment of forgetfulness (nisyan). The principle is that forgetfulness does not negate the obligation itself (wujub) in the rights of Allah, but it can be a valid excuse (udhr) for not performing the act. In the rights of people, it is not an excuse because people's rights are respected and not waived by forgetfulness. The distinction is based on the nature: Allah's rights are a trial (ibtilā'), while people's rights are for their benefit. If forgetfulness is prevalent (ghālib), such as in fasting (where one might forget and eat) or in saying 'Bismillah' at slaughter (where one might forget due to habit), it is pardoned in Allah's rights. However, in other acts, forgetfulness is not an excuse unless it is common (like forgetting the greeting salaam in prayer, which is prevalent). Forgetfulness is divided into two types: original (asli) which is involuntary, and due to negligence (taqsir), which is blameworthy. The text also mentions that analogical extension (ta'diya) from the two mentioned cases (fasting and slaughter) to other cases is not valid because the prevalence is not the same.

Key Terms
النسيان (nisyan): An impediment that does not negate obligation but may be an excuse in certain cases.
الضرب الأصلي (darb asli): Original forgetfulness, involuntary and not due to negligence.
الضرب بالتقصير (darb bi al-taqsir): Forgetfulness due to negligence, suitable for reproach.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is forgetfulness considered an excuse in the rights of Allah?
A) When it occurs in any act of worship.
B) When it is original and prevalent, such as in fasting and slaughter.
C) When it is due to negligence.
D) It is never an excuse.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness in Hanafi usul is an excuse in rights of Allah only when it is original and prevalent; it is never an excuse in rights of people.

The Legal Definition of Sleep and Its Effects
Defining sleep and its legal effects on obligation and actions of the tongue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sleep (nawm) as a legal impediment, explain why it delays but does not cancel obligation, and apply the Hanafi rule that sleep negates choice to determine the validity of statements and actions during sleep.

Core Idea
Sleep negates choice but not obligation — it delays performance without lifting the duty.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi examines the legal definition of sleep (nawm). The author explains that sleep is a state of inability to use one's faculties, which delays the requirement to perform obligatory acts but does not cancel the obligation itself, because sleep is temporary. Sleep also completely negates legal choice (ikhtiyar), rendering any verbal utterances (divorce, emancipation, religious declarations) void. The passage then goes into specific rulings for actions during sleep, especially in prayer, highlighting an intra-Hanafi dispute on loud laughter (qahqaha). Understanding this definition is crucial for distinguishing between impediments that remove obligation and those that merely delay it.

Guided Path
1
Define sleep as a legal impediment
Identify the author's definition: sleep is inability to use the power of states (quwwat al-ahwal). Understand that this definition frames sleep as a temporary incapacity, not a permanent one.
Quwwat al-ahwal refers to the ability to exercise choice and awareness.
2
Analyze the effect on obligation
See how the author argues that sleep delays the address for immediate performance but does not lift the obligation because sleep is short-lived and qada (make-up) is not burdensome.
The hadith 'Whoever sleeps past a prayer... let him pray when he remembers' is cited as proof.
3
Examine the negation of choice
The text states sleep negates choice completely, so any statements (divorce, manumission, etc.) are void. Understand the principle: actions of the tongue require conscious intent; sleep removes that intent.
This is a core Hanafi principle: sleep is a mubtil (invalidator) for statements requiring intent.
4
Explore specific prayer rulings
Note the three cases: recitation (invalid), speech (does not break prayer), laughter (qahqaha) — three opinions. Identify the correct view: no hadath and no invalidation because sleep nullifies the ruling of speech.
The author's tarjih is based on the rationale that laughter's ugliness is excused in sleep.
5
Apply the definition to novel scenarios
Given the definition, test other actions: e.g., contracts, oaths, or testimony made during sleep. Are they valid? No, because choice is absent.
This expands the principle beyond the examples given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النوم : فعَجز عن استعمال قدرة الأحوال، فأوجب تأخير الخطاب للأداء، ولم يمنع الوجوب لاحتمال الأداء؛ لأن النوم لا يمتد، فلا يكون في وجوب القضاء عليه حرج، وإذا كان كذلك: لم يسقط الوجوب. قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: مَن نام عن صلاة، أو نسيها: فليصلها إذا ذكرها» (۱) : فإن ذلك وقتها. وينافي الاختيار أصلاً، حتى بطلت عباراته في الطلاق، والعتاق، والإسلام، والردة، وغير ذلك. والمصلي إذا قرأ في صلاته وهو نائم في حال قيامه : لم تصح قراءته. وإذا تكلم النائم في صلاته : لم تفسد صلاته. وإذا قهقه النائمُ في صلاته فقد قيل : تفسد صلاته، ويكون حدثاً، : وقيل : تفسد صلاته، ولا يكون حدثاً، وقيل: يكون حدثاً، ولا تفسد صلاته، والصحيح أنه لا يكون حدثاً ؛ لأن القهقهة جعلت حدثاً؛ لقُبحها في موضع المناجاة، وسقط ذلك بالنوم، ولا تفسد الصلاة أيضاً؛ لأن النوم يُبطل حكم الكلام.
As for sleep: it is inability to use the power of states, so it necessitates delaying the address for performance, and it does not prevent obligation due to possibility of performance, because sleep does not extend [indefinitely], so there is no difficulty in making up the prayer. If it is so, obligation does not lapse. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it' (1): that is its time. And it negates choice completely, so his statements become void in divorce, manumission, Islam, apostasy, and other matters. If a sleeping person recites in his prayer while standing, his recitation is not valid. If he speaks in his prayer, his prayer is not invalidated. If he laughs loudly (qahqaha) in his prayer, it is said: his prayer is invalidated and it is a hadath; and it is said: his prayer is invalidated but it is not a hadath; and it is said: it is a hadath but his prayer is not invalidated. The correct position is that it is not a hadath because laughter was made a hadath due to its ugliness in the place of intimate conversation, and that is dropped due to sleep, and his prayer is also not invalidated because sleep nullifies the ruling of speech.
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage discusses the impediment of sleep (nawm). The author explains that sleep is an inability to use one's faculties, so the legal address (khitab) for immediate performance is delayed, but the obligation itself remains because sleep is temporary and the person can make up later. The hadith confirms that one must pray when remembered. Sleep completely negates choice (ikhtiyar), so any statements made during sleep (divorce, emancipation, becoming Muslim, apostasy) are void. Specific rules in prayer: if a sleeping person recites, it is not valid; if he speaks, it does not break the prayer; if he laughs (qahqaha), there are three opinions: the correct one according to the author is that it does not break prayer nor is it a hadath, because sleep nullifies the effect of speech and the ugliness of laughter is dropped.

Key Terms
النوم (nawm): Inability to use the power of states (quwwat al-ahwal), delaying obligation but not negating it.
القهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter, normally a hadath and nullifier of prayer when awake.
الحدث (hadath): A state of ritual impurity that necessitates wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It invalidates the prayer but is not a hadath.
C) It is a hadath but does not invalidate the prayer.
D) It does not invalidate the prayer nor is it a hadath.

Key Takeaway
Sleep delays performance of obligations but does not cancel them, and completely negates choice, rendering all verbal acts void.

Legal Effects of Sleep and Unconsciousness in Hanafi Usul
Usul discourse on sleep and coma as affecting capacity and worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul principles (amm, istihsan, qiyas) to derive rulings for sleep and coma, and distinguish their legal effects on worship and capacity.

Core Idea
Sleep is a natural break of choice; coma is a disease that can drop obligations by istihsan.

How does sleep affect your prayers? And what if you fall into a coma? The Hanafi school distinguishes between these two states using key usul tools. This lesson unpacks the hadith on missed prayers and the role of istihsan in overriding strict analogy, helping you derive rulings that balance textual evidence with human hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and classify its text
Locate the hadith cited: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers.' Classify the command 'let him pray it' as amm (general) in Hanafi usul.
The general command indicates obligation (wujub) per the principle 'al-amm yufidu al-wujub'.
2
Derive the ruling for sleep
Apply the hadith: the obligation to make up a missed prayer is not dropped by sleep. The time of remembrance becomes the time for performance.
Sleep nullifies choice but not the underlying obligation.
3
Analyze the differences between sleep and coma
Note that coma is a disease that nullifies strength and is always a hadath, whereas sleep is not inherently a hadath unless accompanied by relaxation.
Coma is more severe and can extend, creating potential hardship.
4
Apply istihsan over qiyas for extended coma
Qiyas to sleep would require making up all prayers. But istihsan (juristic preference) drops the obligation if coma exceeds a day and a night, due to hardship.
This is a key Hanafi departure from strict analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يكون في وجوب القضاء عليه حرج، وإذا كان كذلك: لم يسقط الوجوب. قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: مَن نام عن صلاة، أو نسيها: فليصلها إذا ذكرها (١): فإن ذلك وقتها.
وينافي الاختيار أصلاً، حتى بطلت عباراته في الطلاق، والعتاق، والإسلام، والردة، وغير ذلك.
والمصلي إذا قرأ في صلاته وهو نائم في حال قيامه : لم تصح قراءته.
وإذا تكلم النائم في صلاته : لم تفسد صلاته.
وإذا قهقه النائمُ في صلاته فقد قيل : تفسد صلاته، ويكون حدثاً، وقيل : تفسد صلاته، ولا يكون حدثاً، وقيل: يكون حدثاً، ولا تفسد صلاته، والصحيح أنه لا يكون حدثاً ؛ لأن القهقهة جعلت حدثاً؛ لقُبحها في موضع المناجاة، وسقط ذلك بالنوم، ولا تفسد الصلاة أيضاً؛ لأن النوم يُبطل حكم الكلام.
وأما الإغماء : فإنه ضَرْبُ مرض ، وفَوْتُ قوة، حتى كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم غير معصوم عنه (٢)
(١) باب الأمور المعترضة على الأهلية حديث مَن نام عن صلاة: تقدم في باب بيان صفة حكم الأمر [ص١٣٢].
(٢) قوله : حتى كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم غير معصوم عنه: «عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت : ثَقُل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: أصلى الناس؟ قلنا : لا، هم ينتظرونك يا رسول الله ، قال : ضعوا لي ماءً في المخضب، قالت: ففعلنا، فاغتسل ثم ذهب لينوء فأغمي عليه». الحديث متفق عليه.
وإنما الإغماء في فَوْت الاختيار، وفَوْتِ استعمال القدرة: مثل النوم، حتى مَنَعَ صحة العبادات، وهو أشدُّ منه ؛ لأن النوم فترة أصلية، وهذا عارض ينافي القوة أصلاً.
ألا يُرى أن النائم إذا كان مستقراً: لم يكن نومه حدثاً؛ لأنه يوجب الاسترخاء، لا محالة، والإغماء بكل حال يكون حدثاً، والنوم لازم بأصل الخلقة، وكان النوم من المضطجع في الصلاة إذا لم يتعمده حدثاً لا يمنع البناء. والإغماء من العوارض النادرة في الصلاة وهو فوق الحدث، فلم يكن يُلحق به، ومنع البناء على كل حال.
ويختلفان فيما يجب من حقوق الله تعالى جبراً؛ لأن الإغماء مرض ينافي القوة أصلاً، وقد يحتمل الامتداد على وجه يوجب الحرج، فيسقط به الأداء، وإذا بطل الأداء بطل الوجوب على ما قلنا، وهذا استحسان، وكان القياس أن لا يسقط به شيء من الواجبات، مثل النوم.
وامتداده في الصلوات أن يزيد على يوم وليلة (١)، على ما فسرنا،
(١) [وفي نُسَخ : القدرة. سائد.]
(٢) قوله : امتداده في الصلوات : أن يزيد على يوم وليلة : كأنه يشير إلى ما روى محمد بن الحسن في كتاب «الآثار»: «أنا أبو حنيفة عن حماد عن إبراهيم عن ابن عمر أنه قال في الذي يُغمى عليه يوماً وليلة قال: يقضي.
وروى ابن أبي شيبة عنه : «أنه أغمي عليه يومين : فلم يقض».
وروى سعيد بن منصور أنا أبو معشر عن سعد بن أبي سعيد ومحمد بن قيس ...
There is no difficulty in the obligation of making it up upon him, and if it is so, the obligation is not dropped. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer, or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it' (1): for that is its time. And it contradicts choice fundamentally, so that his expressions become invalid in divorce, manumission, Islam, apostasy, and other things. And the praying person, if he recites in his prayer while he is sleeping during his standing, his recitation is not valid. And if a sleeping person speaks in his prayer, his prayer is not invalidated. And if a sleeping person laughs loudly in his prayer, it has been said: his prayer is invalidated and it is a hadath; and it was said: his prayer is invalidated but it is not a hadath; and it was said: it is a hadath but his prayer is not invalidated; and the correct (opinion) is that it is not a hadath, because loud laughter was made a hadath due to its ugliness in the place of intimate supplication, and that falls away by sleep, and the prayer is also not invalidated because sleep nullifies the ruling of speech. As for unconsciousness (coma), it is a type of illness and a loss of strength, such that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was not infallible from it (2). (1) Chapter on incidental matters affecting capacity: hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer' previously in the chapter on the description of the ruling of command [p.132]. (2) His saying: 'such that the Prophet was not infallible from it': from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah became heavy (ill). He said: Have the people prayed? We said: No, they are waiting for you, O Messenger of Allah. He said: Put water in the tub for me. She said: So we did, then he performed ghusl and went to lift [himself] and fell unconscious.' The hadith is agreed upon. And unconsciousness (coma) is in the loss of choice and the loss of using ability, like sleep, such that it prevents the validity of worship, and it is more severe than it, because sleep is an original period, while this is an incidental occurrence that contradicts strength fundamentally. Do you not see that the sleeping person, if he is settled, his sleep is not a hadath, because it necessarily causes relaxation, but unconsciousness is in every case a hadath. And sleep is inherent in the original constitution, and the sleep of one lying down in prayer, if he did not intend it, is a hadath that does not prevent building (upon previous prayer). And unconsciousness is among the rare incidental occurrences in prayer and is above the hadath, so it is not likened to it, and it prevents building in all circumstances. And they differ regarding what is due of the rights of Allah as compensation, because unconsciousness is an illness that contradicts strength fundamentally, and it may possibly extend in a way that causes difficulty, so performance drops, and if performance drops, the obligation drops as we said. And this is istihsan, and the analogy would be that nothing of the obligations drops by it, like sleep. And its extent in prayers is that it exceeds one day and one night (1), as we explained. (1) [In some copies: 'ability' (al-qudra).] (2) His saying: 'its extent in prayers is that it exceeds one day and one night': as if he is referring to what Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated in the book al-Athar: 'Abu Hanifa narrated to us from Hammad from Ibrahim from Ibn Umar that he said regarding one who falls unconscious for a day and a night: He makes up (the prayer). And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from him: 'He was unconscious for two days and did not make up.' And Sa'id ibn Mansur narrated: Abu Ma'shar from Sa'd ibn Abi Sa'id and Muhammad ibn Qays...
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-oriented discourse on the legal effects of sleep and unconsciousness (coma) in Hanafi usul. It begins by affirming that missing a prayer due to sleep or forgetfulness does not drop the obligation to make it up; the Prophet's hadith is cited as proof, which considers the time of remembrance as the time for performance. The text then explains that sleep nullifies 'choice' (ikhtiyar), rendering invalid any verbal expressions related to legal acts like divorce or manumission. It details specific rulings for a sleeping person in prayer: recitation is invalid, speech does not invalidate the prayer, and loud laughter (qahqaha) is debated—the correct position is that it neither makes it a hadath nor invalidates the prayer, because sleep nullifies the effective ruling of speech. The discussion shifts to unconsciousness (ighma'), which is defined as a type of illness and loss of strength, even affecting prophets. Unconsciousness is compared to sleep in that it nullifies choice and ability, but it is more severe: sleep is a natural state, while coma is an acquired defect. A key distinction is that sleep is not a hadath unless accompanied by relaxation from a lying position, while coma is always a hadath and prevents continuation of prayer. In terms of compensating obligatory acts of worship, coma may drop the obligation of performance due to hardship if it extends beyond a day and a night; this is based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than qiyas (analogy) to sleep. The text also notes the conditions for dropping obligation and mentions differing narrations from Ibn Umar regarding the extent.

Key Terms
النوم (al-nawm): A natural, inherent state of rest that nullifies choice (ikhtiyar) but is not inherently a hadath.
الإغماء (al-ighma'): An acquired illness that nullifies choice and ability, more severe than sleep, always a hadath.
الحدث (al-hadath): A state of ritual impurity that requires ablution; in this passage, it discusses whether sleep or laughter cause hadath.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to hardship or need; used to drop obligations for extended coma.
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter; normally invalidates prayer and is a hadath, but in sleep the ruling drops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct ruling regarding a person who laughs loudly (qahqaha) while sleeping during prayer?
A) The prayer is invalidated and it becomes a hadath.
B) The prayer is invalidated but it does not become a hadath.
C) It becomes a hadath but the prayer is not invalidated.
D) Neither the prayer is invalidated nor does it become a hadath.

Key Takeaway
Sleep does not drop the obligation to make up prayers, but extended coma may drop it by istihsan due to hardship.

The Validity of an Interdicted Slave's Confession: A Three-Way Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of an interdicted slave's confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on an interdicted slave's confession and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
An interdicted slave's confession is valid in hudud but not in property according to Abu Yusuf; Abu Hanifa says both valid; Muhammad says neither.

This lesson examines a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal capacity of an interdicted slave (al-mahjoor). The disagreement hinges on the degree to which a slave's agency is curtailed when interdicted from trade. Understanding this ikhtilaf deepens your appreciation of how capacity (ahliyyah) is graded in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three imams' positions
State what each of the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rules regarding the confession of an interdicted slave in hudud and financial matters.
Refer to the Arabic text: 'عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله بهما، وعند محمد رحمه الله لا يصح بهما، وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يصح بالحد دون المال'.
2
Determine the basis of each position
Consider the implicit rationale: Abu Hanifa sees the slave's capacity as not entirely negated; Muhammad sees it as completely lacking; Abu Yusuf distinguishes between bodily (hudud) and financial matters.
The text does not provide explicit evidence; this is talil based on the school's principles.
3
Apply to a scenario
Imagine an interdicted slave confesses to theft and the stolen property is consumed. Under each imam's view, is the hadd enforced? Is financial restitution required?
This thamarah al-khilaf: for Abu Hanifa, both hadd and compensation; for Muhammad, neither; for Abu Yusuf, hadd but not compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثل شهادته بهلال رمضان وعلى هذا الأصل صح إقراره بالحدود والقصاص، وصح بالسرقة المستهلكة، وبالقائمة صح من المأذون. يصح. وفي المحجور اختلاف معروف عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله بهما، وعند محمد رحمه الله لا يصح بهما، وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يصح بالحد دون المال، وذلك إذا كذبه المولى. وعلى هذا الأصل قلنا في جنايات العبد خطاً: إن رقبته تصير جزاء؛ لأن العبد ليس من أهل ضمان ما ليس بمال ولكنه صلة، إلا أن يشاء المولى الفداء: فيصير عائداً إلى الأصل عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، حتى لا يبطل بالإفلاس، وعندهما يصير بمعنى الحوالة. وهذا أصل لا تُحصى فروعه والله أعلم.
Like his testimony about the crescent of Ramadan, and based on this principle his confession regarding hadd punishments and qisas is valid, and regarding stolen property that is consumed is valid, and regarding what is present it is valid from the permitted slave. It is valid. Regarding the interdicted slave, there is a well-known difference: according to Abu Hanifah, may Allah have mercy on him, both are valid; according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, neither is valid; according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, it is valid for hadd but not for property, and that is when the master denies him. Based on this principle we said regarding unintentional crimes of a slave: his neck becomes compensation; because the slave is not capable of guaranteeing that which is not property but is a gift, unless the master wishes ransom: then it reverts to the principle according to Abu Hanifah, such that it is not invalidated by insolvency, whereas according to the two it becomes like a transfer of debt. And this is a principle whose branches are uncountable, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 734

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal capacity of a slave in three areas: testimony, confession (iqrar), and criminal liability. It states that a slave's testimony regarding the appearance of the Ramadan crescent is valid, and that his confession in hadd punishments (like theft) and qisas is also valid, as well as confession regarding property that has been consumed or is still present, provided the slave is permitted to trade (ma'dhun). For an interdicted slave (mahjoor), there is a three-way disagreement among the Hanafi imams: Imam Abu Hanifa holds his confession valid in both hadd and financial matters; Imam Muhammad holds it invalid in both; and Imam Abu Yusuf holds it valid in hadd but not financial matters when the master denies permission. Regarding unintentional crimes, the principle is that the slave's own neck (i.e., his value or labor) becomes compensation, because a slave is not liable for something that is not property but is a gratuitous obligation (silah). However, if the master chooses to ransom by paying compensation, then according to Abu Hanifa the liability reverts to the master and is not invalidated by the master's insolvency (like a debt), whereas according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it becomes like a transfer of debt (hawalah).

Key Terms
المحجور (al-mahjoor): The interdicted slave, i.e., one not permitted to trade by his master.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession or admission of a right or liability.
الجزاء (al-jaza'): Compensation or reparation, here referring to the slave's value or labor as payment for crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifah regarding the confession of an interdicted slave in hudud and financial matters?
A) Valid in hudud only
B) Valid in both hudud and financial matters
C) Invalid in both
D) Valid in financial matters only

Key Takeaway
An interdicted slave's confession is subject to a three-way Hanafi ikhtilaf based on the degree of capacity recognized.

Slave's Liability for Unintentional Crimes: Compensation Through Value (Raqabah)
Explains the principle of slave liability through his value and the ikhtilaf on master's ransom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a slave's 'neck' becomes compensation for unintentional crimes and identify the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the master's ransom.

Core Idea
A slave's liability for unintentional crimes is through his value, not a financial debt from the master, unless the master chooses to ransom.

This lesson explores a key principle in Hanafi criminal law: the status of a slave as property means that his person (raqabah) secures compensation for his accidental torts. The discussion also reveals a subtle difference between Abu Hanifa and his disciples on the nature of the master's ransom.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base principle
The text states: 'إن رقبته تصير جزاء' — the slave's neck becomes compensation. Recognize that the slave himself is property, so his value covers the damage.
This is because the slave is not capable of guaranteeing something that is not property (ghayr mal) but a gratuitous obligation (silah).
2
Identify the master's option
The master may ransom (fida') by paying compensation, which reverts the liability to him. Note the difference: according to Abu Hanifa, this ransom is like a fixed debt that isn't invalidated by insolvency; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it becomes like a transfer of debt (hawalah).
This distinction affects whether the master's insolvency matters.
3
Apply the principle
Consider a scenario: a slave accidentally kills someone. The victim's family can claim the slave's value from the master. If the master chooses to pay full compensation, under Abu Hanifa the master remains liable even if bankrupt, whereas under the two, if the master is bankrupt, the claim might revert to the slave (like hawalah).
The text says: 'حتى لا يبطل بالإفلاس' for Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثل شهادته بهلال رمضان وعلى هذا الأصل صح إقراره بالحدود والقصاص، وصح بالسرقة المستهلكة، وبالقائمة صح من المأذون. يصح. وفي المحجور اختلاف معروف عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله بهما، وعند محمد رحمه الله لا يصح بهما، وعند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يصح بالحد دون المال، وذلك إذا كذبه المولى. وعلى هذا الأصل قلنا في جنايات العبد خطاً: إن رقبته تصير جزاء؛ لأن العبد ليس من أهل ضمان ما ليس بمال ولكنه صلة، إلا أن يشاء المولى الفداء: فيصير عائداً إلى الأصل عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، حتى لا يبطل بالإفلاس، وعندهما يصير بمعنى الحوالة. وهذا أصل لا تُحصى فروعه والله أعلم.
Like his testimony about the crescent of Ramadan, and based on this principle his confession regarding hadd punishments and qisas is valid, and regarding stolen property that is consumed is valid, and regarding what is present it is valid from the permitted slave. It is valid. Regarding the interdicted slave, there is a well-known difference: according to Abu Hanifah, may Allah have mercy on him, both are valid; according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, neither is valid; according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, it is valid for hadd but not for property, and that is when the master denies him. Based on this principle we said regarding unintentional crimes of a slave: his neck becomes compensation; because the slave is not capable of guaranteeing that which is not property but is a gift, unless the master wishes ransom: then it reverts to the principle according to Abu Hanifah, such that it is not invalidated by insolvency, whereas according to the two it becomes like a transfer of debt. And this is a principle whose branches are uncountable, and Allah knows best.

It states that a slave's testimony regarding the appearance of the Ramadan crescent is valid, and that his confession in hadd punishments (like theft) and qisas is also valid, as well as confession regarding property that has been consumed or is still present, provided the slave is permitted to trade (ma'dhun). المحجور (al-mahjoor): The interdicted slave, i.e., one not permitted to trade by his master.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession or admission of a right or liability.

A) The liability is transferred to the slave.
B) The liability becomes a debt on the master that is not invalidated by insolvency.
C) The liability is cancelled entirely.

Effect of Illness on Legal Capacity and Transactions
Explains how illness affects legal capacity, creating restrictions on transactions for the protection of heirs and creditors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that illness creates interdiction (hajr) to protect heirs and creditors, and distinguish between rescindable and non-rescindable transactions.

Core Idea
Terminal illness does not abolish capacity but restricts transactions to one-third for protecting heirs and creditors.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's usul explains how terminal illness (marad al-mawt) interacts with legal capacity. While illness does not negate the basic capacity to have rulings apply or to perform transactions, it triggers a protective interdiction. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping Hanafi rules on gifts, bequests, and manumission by the ill.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two capacities
The text mentions ahliyat al-hukm (capacity to receive rulings) and ahliyat al-'ibarah (capacity to transact). Note that illness does not negate either.
These terms are foundational in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the rationale for interdiction
Illness leads to death, and death transfers property to heirs/creditors. Thus, their rights attach to the patient's wealth, requiring restrictions.
Interdiction (hajr) is imposed to safeguard these rights.
3
Classify transactions
Distinguish between transactions that can be rescinded (e.g., gifts, sales with overprice) and those that cannot (e.g., manumission). The former are initially valid but may be nullified; the latter are treated as occurring at death and limited to one-third.
This classification is the core of the rule.
4
Note exceptions and specific rulings
Bequests are permitted up to one-third by istihsan, confessions to heirs are void, and valuations are made to prevent fraud.
These are practical applications of the principle.
5
Compare with pledgor's manumission
The ill person's manumission is restricted because heirs have a right in the corpus; the pledgor's manumission is effective because the pledgee only has a right in possession.
This illustrates the scope of interdiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المرض : فإنه لا ينافي أهلية الحكم، ولا أهلية العبارة، ولكنه لما كان سبب الموت والموتُ عجز خالص كان المرض من أسباب العجز، ولما كان الموتُ علةَ الخلافة كان المرض من أسباب تعلق حق الوارث والغريم بماله ولما كان عجزاً شرعت العبادات عليه بقدر المكنة. ولما كان من أسباب تعلق الحقوق كان من أسباب الحجر بقدر ما تقع به صيانة الحق، حتى لا يؤثر المرضُ فيما لا يتعلق به حقٌّ غريم، ولا وارث، وإنما يثبت به الحَجْر إذا اتصل بالموت مستنداً إلى أوله. فقيل : كل تصرف واقع يحتمل الفسخ فإن القول بصحته واجب للحال ، ثم التدارك بالنقض إن احتيج إليه، مثل الهبة، وبيع المحاباة. وكل تصرف لا يحتمل النقض : جعل كالمتعلق بالموت ؛ كالإعتاق إذا وقع على حق غريم أو وارث، وكان القياس أن لا يملك المريض الإيصاء؛ لما قلنا، لكن الشرع جوز ذلك؛ نظراً له بقدر الثلث؛ استخلاصاً على الورثة بالقليل ؛ ليُعلم أن الحجر والتهمة فيه أصل. ولما تولى الشرع الإيصاء للورثة، وأبطل إيصاءه لهم: بطل ذلك صورةً ومعنى، وحقيقةً وشبهةً، حتى لا يصح البيع منه أصلاً عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ، وبطلت أقاريره لهم ؛ للتهمة؛ لأن شبهة الحرام حرام. ولم يصح إقراره باستيفاء دينه من الوارث وإن لزمه في صحته، وتقومت الجَوْدة في حقهم ؛ لتهمة العدول عن خلاف الجنس إلى الجنس، كما تقومت في حق الصغار، وحجر المريض عن الصلة إلا من الثلث ؛ لما قلنا. ولذلك قلنا: إذا أدى في مرض موته حقاً الله تعالى مالياً كان من الثلث ، وكذلك إذا أوصى بذلك عندنا. ولما تعلق حق الغرماء والورثة بالمال صورةً ومعنى في حق أنفسهم، ومعنى في حق غيرهم صار إعتاقه واقعاً على محل مشغول بعينه، بخلاف إعتاق الراهن؛ لأن حق المرتهن في ملك اليد دون ملك الرقبة، فلذلك نَفَذَ هذا ، ولم ينفذ ذلك، وهذا أصل لا تُحصى فروعه
As for illness: it does not contradict legal capacity of ruling nor capacity of expression, but since it is a cause of death, and death is pure incapacity, illness is a cause of incapacity; and since death is the cause of inheritance, illness is a cause of the attachment of the right of the heir and creditor to his property; and since it is incapacity, devotional acts are prescribed upon him to the extent of ability. And since it is a cause of attachment of rights, it is a cause of interdiction to the extent that protection of right occurs, such that illness has no effect on that which no right of creditor or heir attaches; and interdiction is established by it only if it is connected to death, tracing back to its beginning. So it is said: Every transaction that takes place that is susceptible to rescission, the ruling of its validity is obligatory for the present, then remedy by nullification if needed, such as gift and sale with overprice (muhabah). And every transaction that is not susceptible to nullification: it is treated as connected to death; like manumission if it falls upon a right of a creditor or heir. And by analogy the ill person should not have the right to make a bequest, due to what we said, but the law permitted that out of consideration for him up to one third, as a favor to the heirs with little, so that it be known that interdiction and suspicion have a basis in it. And since the law undertook the bequest for the heirs and nullified his bequest to them, that is void in form and meaning, reality and semblance, such that the sale from him is absolutely not valid according to Abu Hanifah, and his confessions in their favor are void due to suspicion; because the semblance of the forbidden is forbidden. And his confession of having received his debt from an heir is not valid even if it was binding upon him in health; and the excellence (value) is assessed against them due to suspicion of deviating from a different type to the same type, as it is assessed against minors. And the ill person is interdicted from gratuitous transfers except from one third, due to what we said. Therefore we said: if he pays a financial obligation to Allah in his terminal illness, it is from the third; likewise if he bequeaths it in our school. And when the right of creditors and heirs attaches to the property in form and meaning in respect of themselves, and in meaning in respect of others, his manumission occurs on a place occupied by a specific right, unlike the manumission of the pledgor; because the right of the pledgee is in the ownership of possession not the ownership of the neck; therefore this is effective, and that is not. And this is a principle whose branches are uncountable.
Source pages p. 734

Commentary
This passage explains the legal effects of illness (marad) on a person's capacity and transactions. It first differentiates between two types of capacity: ahliyat al-hukm (capacity to receive rulings) and ahliyat al-'ibarah (capacity to execute transactions). Illness does not negate either but, because it leads to death (pure incapacity), it creates an attachment of rights of heirs and creditors to the patient's property. Consequently, it imposes a form of interdiction (hajr) to protect those rights, but only if the illness ends in death. The passage then distinguishes between two categories of transactions: (1) those that can be rescinded (like gifts and sales at a disadvantageous price) which are initially valid but can be nullified later if they harm heirs; and (2) those that cannot be rescinded (like manumission) which are treated as if they occurred at death and thus are restricted to the one-third limit. Interestingly, by qiyas, a terminally ill person should not be allowed to make bequests, but the Lawgiver granted permission up to one-third as a favor. The text also notes that bequests to heirs are void entirely, and the patient's confession in favor of heirs is invalid due to suspicion (tuhmah). The patient cannot confirm receipt of a debt from an heir, and valuations are made against the patient to prevent fraud. All gratuitous transfers are limited to one-third. Finally, the passage compares the manumission by a terminally ill person to that by a pledgor: the former is subject to rights of creditors/heirs, so it is restricted; the latter is only subject to the pledgee's right in possession, so it is effective.

Key Terms
أهلية الحكم (ahliyat al-hukm): The capacity to have legal rulings apply to oneself (e.g., being subject to obligations).
أهلية العبارة (ahliyat al-'ibarah): The capacity to carry out transactions and legal expressions effectively.
الحجر (al-hajr): Legal interdiction restricting a person's ability to dispose of property due to illness or other cause.
التصرف الذي يحتمل الفسخ (al-tasarruf alladhi yahtamil al-faskh): A transaction that can be rescinded or annulled, such as a gift or a sale with overprice.
التصرف الذي لا يحتمل النقض (al-tasarruf alladhi la yahtamil al-naqd): A transaction that cannot be undone, such as manumission; it is treated as if it occurred at death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is a terminally ill person's manumission (i'taq) treated?
A) It is absolutely valid with no restrictions
B) It is void from the outset
C) It is treated as if it occurred at death and thus limited to one-third of the estate
D) It is valid only if made in writing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle: terminal illness does not strip legal capacity but creates interdiction (hajr) to protect heirs and creditors, limiting certain irrevocable transactions to one-third of the estate.

Menstruation and Legal Capacity: A Usul Rule
States that menstruation and postnatal bleeding do not remove legal capacity but affect prayer due to loss of purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why menstruation and postnatal bleeding do not remove legal capacity and how the condition of purity relates to the obligation of prayer.

Core Idea
Menstruation does not remove legal capacity; it only suspends prayer due to loss of purity, reflecting the principle of ease.

This lesson examines a foundational usul rule: temporary physical states like menstruation (hayd) and postnatal bleeding (nifas) do not affect a woman's legal capacity. However, because prayer requires ritual purity, and these states prevent purity, the obligation to pray is lifted. The rule is based on the Sharia's quality of ease (yusr), avoiding hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on capacity
Read the passage: watch for the explicit statement that hayd and nifas do not remove ahliyah 'in any way'.
This is the key usul principle: temporary states do not affect capacity.
2
Identify the condition for prayer
The passage mentions taharah (purity) as a condition (shart) for prayer. Understand that a missing condition means the act is not required.
The condition is external to the act but necessary for its validity.
3
Recognize the role of ease (yusr)
The text notes that prayer is prescribed with ease. The exemption during hayd/nifas is an application of this easing.
Hardship (haraj) would arise if prayer were required despite impurity.
4
Connect condition loss to obligation loss
If the condition (taharah) is lost, the obligation to perform prayer is lifted. This is a standard usul rule: fawt al-shart yufid fawt al-mashrut.
The prayer becomes 'fallen' (saqit) but not sinful to miss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الحيض والنفاس : فإنهما لا يُعدمان أهليةً بوجه، لكن الطهارة للصلاة شرط، وقد شرعت بصفة اليُسر، وفي فَوْت الشرط: فوتُ الأداء، وفي وضع الحيض والنفاس ما يوجب الحرج في
And as for menstruation and postnatal bleeding: they do not remove capacity in any way, but purity is a condition for prayer, and it (prayer) has been prescribed with the quality of ease, and with the loss of the condition comes loss of performance, and in the imposition of menstruation and postnatal bleeding is that which necessitates hardship in...
Source pages p. 735

Commentary
This passage begins a discussion on the legal effect of menstruation (hayd) and postnatal bleeding (nifas). It establishes the fundamental principle that these conditions do not negate a woman's legal capacity (ahliyah) in any respect. However, because ritual purity (taharah) is a condition (shart) for the validity of prayer, and prayer has been prescribed with the attribute of ease, the loss of that condition results in the loss of the obligation to perform prayer (i.e., the prayer is not required). The text suggests that requiring a woman to perform prayer during these states would impose undue hardship. The passage is cut off, but it sets the stage for the detailed rules about exemption from prayer and other acts of worship during menstruation and postpartum bleeding.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): Menstrual bleeding that occurs in women of menstruating age.
النفاس (al-nifas): Postnatal bleeding after childbirth.
أهلية (ahliyah): Legal capacity, the fitness to be subject to legal rights and duties.
الطهارة (al-taharah): Ritual purity, a condition for the validity of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the text say about menstruation (hayd) and postnatal bleeding (nifas) regarding a woman's legal capacity (ahliyah)?
A) They completely remove her legal capacity
B) They do not remove capacity in any way
C) They remove capacity only for financial transactions
D) They remove capacity only for devotional acts

Key Takeaway
Menstruation and postnatal bleeding do not affect legal capacity; prayer is exempted due to loss of purity, not incapacity.

The Principle of Restriction on Terminal Illness
Explaining the usul rule for terminally ill transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul rule that a terminally ill person's transactions are restricted to one-third of the estate, and identify the underlying rationale of protecting heirs and creditors.

Core Idea
A terminally ill person can only give up to one-third; transactions beyond that are suspect and often invalid.

The terminally ill person (marad al-mawt) occupies a unique legal status: his financial capacity is restricted to prevent fraud against heirs and creditors. This lesson unpacks the foundational principle that while analogy would prohibit all gifts, the Law permits up to one-third as a balance. We will explore the rule and its rationale as stated by Imam al-Bazdawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
The passage begins by noting that analogy (qiyas) would suggest that a terminally ill person cannot make any will or gift because his right is restricted. Identify this starting point.
Analogy alone would lead to a harsh ruling, but the Law intervenes.
2
Locate the exception (rukhsah)
The Law (shar‘) permitted the sick person to act up to one-third of his estate as a favor. Find the phrase that indicates this exception and its basis.
The one-third limit is derived from hadith, but here it is presented as a legislative favor.
3
Understand the rationale
The passage explains that this permission is 'extracting from heirs a little' so that restriction is known to be foundational. This shows the balance between the sick person's interest and the heirs' rights.
The concept of 'tuhma' (suspicion) is central—any transaction that appears to favor an heir or creditor is suspect.
4
Distinguish revocable vs. irrevocable acts
The passage divides transactions into those that can be revoked (like gifts) and those that cannot (like manumission). The rule applies differently to each category.
Irrevocable acts are treated as if they take effect at death, so they are restricted.
5
Apply to a concrete case
Consider a sale by a terminally ill person to an heir. According to Abu Hanifa, such a sale is absolutely invalid. Find the text and understand why it is invalid, not just restricted.
The sale is invalid because the semblance of the unlawful is unlawful—the suspect intent taints the transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للحال ، ثم التدارك بالنقض إن احتيج إليه، مثل الهبة، وبيع المحاباة. وكل تصرف لا يحتمل النقض : جعل كالمتعلق بالموت ؛ كالإعتاق إذا وقع على حق غريم أو وارث، وكان القياس أن لا يملك المريض الإيصاء؛ لما قلنا، لكن الشرع جوز ذلك؛ نظراً له بقدر الثلث؛ استخلاصاً على الورثة بالقليل ؛ ليُعلم أن الحجر والتهمة فيه أصل. أبي ولما تولى الشرع الإيصاء للورثة، وأبطل إيصاءه لهم: بطل ذلك صورةً ومعنى، وحقيقةً وشبهةً، حتى لا يصح البيع منه أصلاً عند حنيفة رحمه الله ، وبطلت أقاريره لهم ؛ للتهمة؛ لأن شبهة الحرام حرام. ولم يصح إقراره باستيفاء دينه من الوارث وإن لزمه في صحته، وتقومت الجَوْدة في حقهم ؛ لتهمة العدول عن خلاف الجنس إلى الجنس، كما تقومت في حق الصغار، وحجر المريض عن الصلة إلا من الثلث ؛ لما قلنا. ولذلك قلنا: إذا أدى في مرض موته حقاً الله تعالى مالياً كان من الثلث ، وكذلك إذا أوصى بذلك عندنا. ولما تعلق حق الغرماء والورثة بالمال صورةً ومعنى في حق أنفسهم، ومعنى في حق غيرهم صار إعتاقه واقعاً على محل مشغول بعينه، بخلاف إعتاق الراهن؛ لأن حق المرتهن في ملك اليد دون ملك الرقبة، فلذلك نَفَذَ هذا ، ولم ينفذ ذلك، وهذا أصل لا تُحصى فروعه
For the current state, then rectification by revocation if needed, such as gift and undervalued sale. Every transaction that does not admit revocation is treated as related to death, like manumission if it affects a right of a creditor or heir. The analogical reasoning would be that a sick person cannot make a will, due to what we said, but the Sacred Law permitted it for him up to one-third, as a favor to him, extracting from the heirs a little, so that it may be known that restriction and suspicion are foundational. And when the Law took charge of the will for the heirs and nullified his will to them, it became void in form and meaning, reality and semblance, so that a sale from him is absolutely invalid according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and his acknowledgments to them are void due to suspicion, because the semblance of the unlawful is unlawful. And his acknowledgment of discharging his debt from the heir is not valid even if it was incumbent upon him in health, and the quality is evaluated in their favor due to suspicion of deviation from a different category to the same category, as it is evaluated in favor of minors. And the sick person is restricted from giving gratuitously except from the one-third, due to what we said. Therefore we said: If he pays, during his terminal illness, a financial right of Allah Almighty, it is from the one-third, and likewise if he bequeaths it according to us. And when the right of creditors and heirs attaches to property, in form and meaning regarding themselves, and in meaning regarding others, his manumission occurs on a place occupied by a specific title, unlike the manumission of a pledgor, because the right of the pledgee is over the right of possession (yad) and not over the right of ownership (raqaba). Therefore this (the sick person's manumission) is invalid, while that (the pledgor's) is valid. And this is a fundamental principle whose branches are countless.
Source pages p. 735

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling on the restrictions placed on a terminally ill person (marad al-mawt) regarding financial transactions. The author, Imam al-Bazdawi, explains that while analogy would suggest that a terminally ill person cannot make any will or gift because his right is restricted, the Law allows him to act up to one-third of his estate as a favor. This is to balance his interests against those of heirs and creditors. The principle is that any transaction that can be revoked (like gifts) is subject to revision, but those that cannot be revoked (like manumission) are treated as if they apply at the time of death. For Abu Hanifa, if a terminally ill person sells to an heir, the sale is absolutely invalid due to suspicion (tuhma). Similarly, acknowledgments of debt to heirs are void. Payments of financial obligations to Allah (like zakat) during terminal illness are from the one-third, as are bequests. The passage contrasts with a pledgor's manumission, which is valid because the pledgee's right is only over possession, not ownership. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding the legal capacity of the terminally ill.

Key Terms
المريض مرض الموت (al-marīḍ maraḍ al-mawt): A person suffering from a terminal illness that is likely to lead to death, whose legal capacity is restricted in financial transactions to protect heirs and creditors.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum limit for bequests and charitable acts by a terminally ill person, as per the juristic principle of preserving heirs' shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the maximum amount a terminally ill person can give away without needing heirs' consent?
A) He can give away his entire estate if he wishes.
B) He can give away up to one-third of his estate.
C) He can give away only what is necessary for his treatment.
D) He cannot give away anything because his capacity is suspended.

Key Takeaway
The fundamental Hanafi rule: a terminally ill person may dispose of up to one-third of his estate; transactions exceeding this or involving suspicion of fraud are invalid.

Applications and Exceptions in Marad al-Mawt
Applying the usul rule to specific transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of restriction in terminal illness to specific transactions (sale, manumission, acknowledgment) and distinguish the Hanafi position from the general analogy.

Core Idea
Irrevocable acts like manumission are treated as testamentary, while revocable gifts are subject to revocation.

The previous lesson established the core rule: the terminally ill may only give up to one-third. Now we delve into specific applications: why a sale to an heir is absolutely invalid, why manumission is restricted, and how acknowledgment of debt is treated. We also compare with a pledgor's case to refine our understanding.

Guided Path
1
Examine the sale to an heir
The passage states that a sale by a terminally ill person to an heir is 'absolutely invalid' according to Abu Hanifa. Identify the reason: suspicion (tuhma).
This is stronger than just restriction; it is total invalidity.
2
Analyze manumission and its effect
Manumission is an irrevocable act. The passage says it is treated as related to death (kalmuta‘alliq bi al-mawt). How does this affect its validity?
It is restricted to one-third and, if it affects creditors/heirs, it is invalid beyond one-third.
3
Understand acknowledgment of debt
The passage says acknowledgments to heirs are void due to suspicion. Why is an acknowledgment of discharging a debt from an heir also invalid?
Because it is equivalent to favoring the heir.
4
Compare with the pledgor
The passage contrasts manumission by a terminally ill person with manumission by a pledgor. Why is the pledgor's manumission valid while the sick person's is not?
The pledgee's right is only over possession (yad), not ownership (raqaba), so the pledgor still owns the slave.
5
Apply the principle to a new case
Suppose a terminally ill person gifts his entire estate to a charity and then dies. The estate has debts. Apply the rule: the gift is valid only up to one-third; debts are paid first.
The gift beyond one-third requires consent of creditors/heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للحال ، ثم التدارك بالنقض إن احتيج إليه، مثل الهبة، وبيع المحاباة. وكل تصرف لا يحتمل النقض : جعل كالمتعلق بالموت ؛ كالإعتاق إذا وقع على حق غريم أو وارث، وكان القياس أن لا يملك المريض الإيصاء؛ لما قلنا، لكن الشرع جوز ذلك؛ نظراً له بقدر الثلث؛ استخلاصاً على الورثة بالقليل ؛ ليُعلم أن الحجر والتهمة فيه أصل. أبي ولما تولى الشرع الإيصاء للورثة، وأبطل إيصاءه لهم: بطل ذلك صورةً ومعنى، وحقيقةً وشبهةً، حتى لا يصح البيع منه أصلاً عند حنيفة رحمه الله ، وبطلت أقاريره لهم ؛ للتهمة؛ لأن شبهة الحرام حرام. ولم يصح إقراره باستيفاء دينه من الوارث وإن لزمه في صحته، وتقومت الجَوْدة في حقهم ؛ لتهمة العدول عن خلاف الجنس إلى الجنس، كما تقومت في حق الصغار، وحجر المريض عن الصلة إلا من الثلث ؛ لما قلنا. ولذلك قلنا: إذا أدى في مرض موته حقاً الله تعالى مالياً كان من الثلث ، وكذلك إذا أوصى بذلك عندنا. ولما تعلق حق الغرماء والورثة بالمال صورةً ومعنى في حق أنفسهم، ومعنى في حق غيرهم صار إعتاقه واقعاً على محل مشغول بعينه، بخلاف إعتاق الراهن؛ لأن حق المرتهن في ملك اليد دون ملك الرقبة، فلذلك نَفَذَ هذا ، ولم ينفذ ذلك، وهذا أصل لا تُحصى فروعه
For the current state, then rectification by revocation if needed, such as gift and undervalued sale. Every transaction that does not admit revocation is treated as related to death, like manumission if it affects a right of a creditor or heir. The analogical reasoning would be that a sick person cannot make a will, due to what we said, but the Sacred Law permitted it for him up to one-third, as a favor to him, extracting from the heirs a little, so that it may be known that restriction and suspicion are foundational. Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling on the restrictions placed on a terminally ill person (marad al-mawt) regarding financial transactions. The author, Imam al-Bazdawi, explains that while analogy would suggest that a terminally ill person cannot make any will or gift because his right is restricted, the Law allows him to act up to one-third of his estate as a favor. This is to balance his interests against those of heirs and creditors. For Abu Hanifa, if a terminally ill person sells to an heir, the sale is absolutely invalid due to suspicion (tuhma). Similarly, acknowledgments of debt to heirs are void. Payments of financial obligations to Allah (like zakat) during terminal illness are from the one-third, as are bequests. The passage contrasts with a pledgor's manumission, which is valid because the pledgee's right is only over possession, not ownership. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh regarding the legal capacity of the terminally ill.

Key Terms
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion or accusation; in Hanafi fiqh, a legal presumption that certain actions are motivated by fraud or favoritism, leading to invalidity.
شبهة الحرام حرام (shubhat al-haram haram): The semblance of the unlawful is unlawful; a legal maxim meaning that anything that closely resembles a prohibited act is itself prohibited.

C) The terminally ill person does not own the slave if he is in debt.
D) The passage does not discuss pledgor's manumission.

Key Takeaway
Specific transactions by a terminally ill person (sale to heir, acknowledgment, manumission) are either absolutely invalid or restricted to one-third, based on the principle of tuhma and the nature of the act.

Death as Total Incapacity: The Lifting of Taklif
Definition of death and its effect on taklif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define death in Hanafi usul as total incapacity and explain why all acts of worship are dropped for the deceased.

Core Idea
Death is total incapacity; all obligations (taklif) are lifted because their purpose is lost.

This lesson introduces the concept of death as a complete barrier to legal capacity in Hanafi usul. The passage from Usul al-Bazdawi states that death negates the capacity for worldly rulings that involve obligation, resulting in all acts of worship being nullified. Understanding this principle is essential for distinguishing between obligations that cease and rights that persist.

Guided Path
1
Define death in Hanafi usul
Look at the phrase 'عجز كله' (total incapacity). Death is not merely an incapacity but a complete one, in contrast to partial incapacity like sickness or slavery.
Hanafis consider death a barrier (mani) that completely removes legal competence.
2
Identify which rulings are affected
The text specifies 'أهلية أحكام الدنيا مما فيه تكليف' – capacity for worldly rulings that involve obligation. This means only rulings with taklif (obligation) are lifted; pure rights or property matters may remain.
Taklif requires a living, competent person.
3
Explain the consequence for acts of worship
All acts of worship (ibadat) are dropped from the deceased. The author gives zakat as an example. However, sin remains for missed obligations because the duty to perform was present before death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الموتُ : فإنه عجز كله، مناف لأهلية أحكام الدنيا مما فيه تكليف، حتى وضعت العبادات كلها عنه. والأحكام نوعان : أحكام الدنيا، وأحكام الآخرة. فأما أحكام الدنيا فأنواع أربعة: الأداء - القسم الأول - منها : ما هو من باب التكليف. والثاني : ما شرع عليه لحاجة غيره. ومنها : ما شرع له لحاجته. ومنها ما لا يصلح لقضاء حاجته، هذه أحكام الدنيا. فأما القسم الأول: فقد وضع عنه الخطاب؛ لفوت غرضه، وهو عن اختيار ولهذا قلنا إن الزكاة تبطل عنه، وكذلك سائر القرب، وإنما يبقى عليه المأثم. وأما القسم الثاني : فإنه إن كان حقاً متعلقاً بالعين: يبقى ببقائه؛ لأن فعله فيه غير مقصود. وإن كان ديناً: لم يبق بمجرد الذمة حتى يُضم إليه مال، أو ما تُؤكَّد به الذمم، وهو ذمة الكفيل؛ لأن ضعف الذمة بالموت فوق الضعف بالرق؛ لأن الرق يرجى زواله غالباً، وهذا لا يُرجى زواله غالباً، فقلنا إنها لا تحتمل الدين بنفسها. ولهذا قيل : إن الكفالة عن الميت المفلس لا تصح، وهو قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، كأن الدين ساقط؛ لأن ثبوته بالمطالبة، والكفالة لالتزام المطالبة، وقد عُدمت. بخلاف العبد المحجور يُقِرُّ بالدين، فتكفل عنه رجل: صح؛ لأن
As for death: it is total incapacity, contradictory to the capacity for worldly rulings that involve obligation, until all acts of worship are dropped from him. And rulings are of two types: rulings of this world and rulings of the Hereafter. As for rulings of this world, they are four types: (1) Performance: the first type: that which falls under obligation. The second: that which is prescribed for the sake of another's need. And among them: that which is prescribed for his own need. And among them: that which is not suitable to fulfill his need – these are the rulings of this world. As for the first type: the address is lifted from him because its purpose is lost, and it is not by choice. Therefore we say that zakat is nullified from him, as well as all other acts of devotion, and only sin remains upon him. As for the second type: if it is a right attached to a physical asset, it remains as long as the asset remains, because his action is not intended in it. And if it is a debt, it does not remain merely by the dhimmah (obligation) until wealth is added to it, or what strengthens the dhimmah, i.e., the guarantee of a surety; because the weakness of the dhimmah due to death is greater than weakness due to slavery; because slavery is usually hoped to be removed, while this is not usually hoped to be removed. So we say that the dhimmah alone does not bear the debt. For this reason it is said that suretyship (kafalah) for a deceased insolvent is not valid – this is the saying of Abu Hanifah, may Allah have mercy on him – as if the debt is dropped because its establishment is through demand, and suretyship is to undertake the demand, but it is absent. Contrary to a slave under interdiction who confesses a debt, then a man becomes his surety: it is valid because
Source pages p. 737

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi discusses the effect of death on legal capacity (ahliyyah). Death is defined as total incapacity, negating the capacity for worldly rulings that involve obligation (taklif). Consequently, all acts of worship fall away from the deceased. The author divides rulings into two broad categories: those of this world (dunya) and those of the Hereafter (akhirah). Rulings of this world are further subdivided into four types: (1) matters of obligation (taklif), (2) those prescribed for the benefit of others, (3) those prescribed for one's own benefit, and (4) those that are not suitable for fulfilling one's need. For the deceased, the first type (obligations) is lifted because the purpose (reward/punishment) is no longer achievable. Thus, obligations like zakat are nullified, and only sin from missed obligations remains. The second type includes rights of others: if it is a right attached to a physical asset (e.g., collateral), it remains with the asset. If it is a debt, it does not persist solely through the dhimmah (personal obligation) unless accompanied by actual wealth or a guarantor (kafalah). This is because the dhimmah of the deceased is weaker than that of a slave (who may become free). Therefore, a debt without assets or surety is considered dropped, as it requires the possibility of demand. Hence, suretyship for a deceased insolvent is invalid according to Abu Hanifah. This is contrasted with a slave under interdiction (mahjur) who confesses a debt—suretyship for him is valid, because his dhimmah is still intact and can be strengthened. The passage ends mid-sentence, continuing the comparison.

Key Terms
الموت (al-mawt): Total incapacity that contradicts legal capacity for worldly rulings involving obligation.
التكليف (al-taklif): The address of the Lawgiver demanding an action from the legally competent person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul definition in this lesson, what happens to the obligation of zakat upon death?
A) It must be paid from the estate.
B) It is nullified, but sin remains.
C) It is transferred to the heirs.
D) It becomes a debt on the deceased's property.

Key Takeaway
Death lifts all obligations (taklif) because it is total incapacity; only sin from missed obligations remains.
